<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><A NAME="tx414521_25"></A>NOTES TO 
CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-
top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>(1) Summary of Significant 
Accounting Policies </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px;
margin-left:2%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2"><B><I></I></B><I>(a)
General</I><B><I> </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-
bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2">Marine Petroleum Trust (the &#147;Trust&#148;) was established on 
June&nbsp;1, 1956 with the
transfer of property to the Trust consisting of certain contract rights, units 
of beneficial interest and common stock in exchange for units of beneficial 
interest in the Trust. The contract rights entitled the Trust to receive an 
overriding royalty
interest in oil, natural gas and other mineral leasehold interests acquired by 
Gulf Oil Corporation, now Chevron U.S.A., Inc. (&#147;Chevron&#148;), a 
subsidiary of Chevron Corporation, in certain areas of the Gulf of Mexico prior 
to January&nbsp;1,
1980. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-
indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Trust must 
distribute all income, after paying its liabilities and obligations, to the 
unitholders during the
months of March, June, September and December each year. The Trust and its 
subsidiary cannot engage in a trade or business. Funds held by Marine Petroleum 
Corporation, a wholly-owned subsidiary of the Trust, (&#147;MPC,&#148; and 
collectively with
the Trust, &#147;Marine&#148;) pending distribution to the Trust are invested in
U.S. Treasury and agency bonds. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-
bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2">The
unitholders assigned their contract rights offshore of Louisiana to MPC 
reserving a 98% net profits interest to themselves. The net profits interest 
contract was transferred to the Trust along with the other properties. The Trust
is authorized to
pay expenses of MPC should it be necessary. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-
top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">The Trust is to continue until June&nbsp;1, 2021, or until such 
later date as
holders of the units owning a majority of the outstanding units may designate, 
but in any event, not more than 20 years from such designation. However, the 
unitholders owning eighty percent (80%)&nbsp;of the outstanding units may 
terminate the Trust
on any date. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-
left:2%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I></I></B><I>(b)
Principles of Consolidation</I><B><I> </I></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The consolidated financial statements include 
the Trust and its wholly-owned subsidiary, MPC. All material intercompany 
accounts and
transactions have been eliminated in consolidation. </FONT></P> <P 
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I></I></B><I>(c) Producing Oil and Gas 
Properties</I><B><I>
</I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-
indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">At the time the 
Trust was established, no determinable market value was available for the assets
transferred to the
Trust; consequently, nominal values were assigned. Accordingly, no allowance for
depletion has been included. All income from oil and natural gas royalties 
relate to proved developed oil and natural gas reserves. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I></I></B><I>(d) U.S. Federal Income 
Taxes</I><B><I> </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; 
text-indent:4%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">No provision has been made for U.S.
Federal income taxes on the Trust&#146;s income since such taxes are the 
liability of the unitholders. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">U.S. Federal income taxes have been provided on
the income of MPC (which specifically excludes the 98% net profits interest to 
be
retained by and&nbsp;delivered to the Trust), after deducting statutory 
depletion. MPC uses the cash method of reporting for U.S. Federal income taxes. 
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The primary difference between the 
actual tax expense of MPC and the expected tax expense is due to the fact that 
only 2% of MPC&#146;s income (i.e., excluding the 98% net profits interest 
retained by,
and delivered to, the Trust) is subject to U.S. Federal income tax. </FONT></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">-28-
</FONT></P>
<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
<h5 align="left"><a href="#toc">Table of Contents</a></h5>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Tax positions taken by the Trust related to the
Trust&#146;s pass-through status and federal
state tax positions have been reviewed, and the Trustee is of the opinion that 
material positions taken would more likely than not be sustained upon an 
examination. In accordance with the Trust&#146;s basis of accounting discussed 
in Note 1, the
Trust would only recognize the impact of tax positions that were not upheld at 
the time of payment. As of June&nbsp;30, 2012, the Trust&#146;s tax years 2008 
and thereafter remain subject to examination. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Federal income taxes refundable which arose
during the prior year are as a result of payments previously made in excess of 
the
estimated taxes payable. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-
bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2">MPC recognizes interest and penalties related to unrecognized tax 
benefits in income tax expense.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT 
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I></I></B><I>(e) Credit Risk 
Concentration and Cash Equivalents</I><B><I> </I></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Financial instruments which potentially subject
Marine to concentrations of credit risk are primarily investments in cash 
equivalents,
U.S. Treasury and agency bonds. The Trust and MPC place their cash investments 
with financial institutions or companies that the Trustee considers credit 
worthy and limit the amount of credit exposure from any one financial 
institution. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Marine had cash and cash equivalents of 
$1,184,244 and $1,345,960 at June&nbsp;30, 2012 and 2011, respectively, which 
consisted of cash
deposits, U.S. Treasury and agency bonds, and money market mutual funds. 
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT 
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I></I></B><I>(f) Use of 
Estimates</I><B><I>
</I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-
indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The preparation of
financial statements in conformity with the modified cash basis method of 
accounting requires the
Trustee to make various estimates and assumptions that affect the reported 
amount of liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported
amount of expenses during the reporting period.&nbsp;Actual results may differ 
from such
estimates. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-
left:2%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I></I></B><I>(g)
Distributable Income per Unit</I><B><I> </I></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Distributable income per unit is determined by 
dividing distributable income by the number of units of beneficial interest 
outstanding
during the period. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; 
margin-left:2%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2"><B><I></I></B><I>(h) Significant Royalty Sources</I><B><I> 
</I></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Percent of royalty revenue received by Marine 
from producers is summarized as follows: </FONT></P>

</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0"

Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times 
New Roman" SIZE="2">Royalty income is recognized in the month received rather 
than in the month of production. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" 
CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times 
New Roman" SIZE="2">Reserves may be established for contingencies that would not
be recorded under GAAP. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" 
CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times 
New Roman" SIZE="2">Expenses are recorded in the month paid rather than in the 
month incurred. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">This comprehensive basis of accounting 
corresponds to the accounting principles permitted for royalty trusts by the 
Securities and
Exchange Commission (the &#147;SEC&#148;), as specified by Staff Accounting 
Bulletin Topic 12:E, Financial Statements of Royalty Trusts. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2"><B>(3) Investment in Affiliate&#151;Tidelands Royalty Trust 
&#147;B&#148; </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-
indent:4%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">At June&nbsp;30, 2012 and 2011, the
Trust owned 32.6% of the outstanding units of beneficial interest in Tidelands 
Royalty Trust &#147;B&#148; (&#147;Tidelands&#148;). The 452,366 units owned by
the Trust
had a quoted market value $2,374,921 and $3,727,496 at June&nbsp;30, 2012 and 
2011, respectively, based on the closing price of Tideland&#146;s units on the 
OTC Bulleting Board on such dates. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Administrative expenses are shared by MPC and 
Tidelands Royalty Trust &#147;B&#148; Corporation, a wholly-owned subsidiary of 
Tidelands,
in the ratio of each of MPC&#146;s and Tidelands Royalty Trust &#147;B&#148; 
Corporation&#146;s gross oil and natural gas royalties to the total gross oil 
and natural gas royalties of both entities. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-

<h5 align="left"><a href="#toc">Table of Contents</a></h5>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2"><B>(6) Texas Margin Tax </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-
top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Texas does not impose an income 
tax. Therefore, no part of the income produced by the Trust is subject to a 
state income tax in Texas. However, in May&nbsp;2006, the State of Texas enacted
legislation, as
amended, to implement a new franchise tax. Under the Texas franchise tax 
statute, a 1% tax (in certain cases not applicable here, the tax rate is 0.5%) 
is imposed on each taxable entity&#146;s taxable margin that is apportioned to 
Texas. Taxable
margin is generally defined as revenues less certain costs, as provided under 
the statute. Most entities that provide owners with limited liability 
protection, including trusts, are considered to be taxable entities for purposes
of the Texas
franchise tax. The statute provides certain limited exemptions from the tax,
including exclusions for certain &#147;passive entities&#148; that satisfy 
specified statutory requirements as described below. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Under the Texas franchise tax statute, 
&#147;passive entities,&#148; including trusts, that meet the following 
requirements, are exempt
from the Texas franchise tax: (a)&nbsp;the trust cannot be a business trust 
within the meaning of U.S. Treasury Regulation section 301.7701-4(b); 
(b)&nbsp;at least 90% of the trust&#146;s income for the taxable year must be 
derived from passive
sources (<I>e.g.</I>, royalties, bonuses, delay rental income from mineral 
properties, dividends, interest, gains from the sale of securities); and 
(c)&nbsp;no more than 10% of the trust&#146;s income for the taxable year can be
derived from an
active trade or business (<I>e.g.</I>, rent, certain income received by a non-
operator under a joint operating agreement pursuant to which the operator is the
member of an affiliated group that includes such non-operator). An entity will 
determine
on an annual basis whether it meets the requirements to be treated as a 
&#147;passive entity&#148; for Texas franchise tax purposes. The Trustee 
believes that all or substantially all of the income of the Trust currently is 
passive, as it consists
of royalty income from the sale of oil and natural gas, dividends and interest 
income. Subject to any change in the sources of income derived by the Trust or 
any change in the Indenture, the Trust expects that it will continue to qualify 
as a
passive entity that is not subject to the franchise tax. </FONT></P> <P 
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">If the Trust is exempt from the Texas franchise
tax as a passive
entity, each unitholder that is subject to the Texas franchise tax as a taxable 
entity under the Texas Tax Code would generally include its share of the 
Trust&#146;s revenue in its franchise tax computation. The Texas franchise tax 
does not apply to
natural persons. The Trust anticipates that it will be a passive entity in the 
tax year ending in 2012. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-
bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2">Each unitholder is
urged to consult its own tax advisor regarding the requirements for filing state
tax returns. </FONT></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">-32-
</FONT></P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="right"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Exhibit 99.1 </B></FONT></P> <P 
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>REPORT OF INDEPENDENT REGISTERED
PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-
bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Trustee and 
Holders of Trust
Units of </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT 
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Tidelands Royalty Trust 
&#147;B&#148; and Subsidiary: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-
bottom:0px"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">We have audited the accompanying
consolidated statement of assets, liabilities, and trust corpus of Tidelands 
Royalty Trust &#147;B&#148; and Subsidiary (the Trust) as of December&nbsp;31, 
2011 and the
related consolidated statements of distributable income and changes in trust 
corpus for the year then ended. These consolidated financial statements are the 
responsibility of the Trustee. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on 
these
consolidated financial statements based on our audit. </FONT></P> <P 
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">We conducted our audit in accordance with standards of the 
Public Company Accounting
Oversight Board (United States). Those standards require that we plan and 
perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the consolidated 
financial statements are free of material misstatement. The Trust is not 
required to have, nor
were we engaged to perform, an audit of its internal control over financial 
reporting. Our audit included consideration of internal control over financial 
reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the 
circumstances,
but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the 
Trust&#146;s internal control over financial reporting. Accordingly, we express 
no such opinion. An audit also includes examining, on a test basis, evidence 
supporting the
amounts and disclosures in the consolidated financial statements, assessing the 
accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management, as well
as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. We believe that our 
audit
provides a reasonable basis for our opinion. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-
top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2">As described in Note 2 to the consolidated financial statements, these 
consolidated financial
statements were prepared on the modified cash basis of accounting, which is a 
comprehensive basis of accounting other than accounting principles generally 
accepted in the United States of America. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">In our opinion, the consolidated financial statements referred 
to above present fairly, in all material respects, the assets, liabilities, and 
trust
corpus of Tidelands Royalty Trust &#147;B&#148; and Subsidiary as of 
December&nbsp;31, 2011, and its distributable income and changes in trust corpus
for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2011 in conformity with the modified cash 
basis of accounting
described in Note 2 to the consolidated financial statements. </FONT></P> <P

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>

<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>TIDELANDS ROYALTY TRUST &#147;B&#148; AND 
SUBSIDIARY </B></FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 
</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>DECEMBER 31, 2011 
</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-
bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" 
CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2"><B>(1)</B></FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2"><B>SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES AND GENERAL 
</B></FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-
indent:8%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">(a) General </FONT></P> <P 
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Tidelands Royalty Trust &#147;B&#148; (the 
&#147;Trust&#148;) was
established on June&nbsp;1, 1954 with a transfer of contract rights to certain 
properties to the Trust in exchange for units of beneficial interest. The 
contract rights enable the Trust to receive an interest in any oil, natural gas 
or other mineral
leases obtained by Gulf Oil Corporation, now Chevron U.S.A., Inc. 
(&#147;Chevron&#148;), which is a subsidiary of Chevron Corporation and its 
assignees in a designated area of the Gulf of Mexico during a 50-year period 
that expired on April&nbsp;30,
2001. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-
indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Trust is 
required under its Indenture to distribute all income, after paying its 
liabilities and obligations, to
the unitholders quarterly. The Trust cannot invest any of its money for any 
purpose and cannot engage in a trade or business. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Trust&#146;s wholly-owned subsidiary, 
Tidelands Royalty &#147;B&#148; Corporation (&#147;Tidelands Corporation&#148;),
holds title to
interests in properties that are situated offshore of Louisiana. Ninety-five 
percent of all oil, natural gas, and other mineral royalties collected by this 
subsidiary are retained by and delivered to the Trust. Tidelands Corporation, 
like the Trust,
is prohibited from engaging in a trade or business and does only those things 
necessary for the administration and liquidation of its properties. The Trust is
authorized to pay the expenses of Tidelands Corporation should it be necessary.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT 
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Trust and its subsidiary have 
no employees. Tidelands Corporation has entered into an arrangement with Marine 
Petroleum
Corporation (a wholly-owned subsidiary of Marine Petroleum Trust, an affiliate 
of the Trust) to share certain administrative expenses and to assist the trustee
in the administration of the Trust. For the years ended 2011, 2010 and 2009, 
Tidelands
Corporation paid $49,000, $54,450 and $48,900 to Marine Petroleum Corporation, 
respectively. At December&nbsp;31, 2011 and 2010, Marine Petroleum Trust owned 
32.6% of the Trust&#146;s outstanding units of beneficial interest. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">(b) Unitholder Voting Matters </FONT></P> <P 
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On March&nbsp;27, 2001, the 
unitholders of record at the close of business on February&nbsp;16, 2001, 
approved an amendment to the Indenture to extend the life of the Trust to 
April&nbsp;30, 2021.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT 
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">(c) Principles of Consolidation 
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The consolidated financial 
statements include the Trust and its wholly-owned subsidiary, Tidelands 
Corporation. All material intercompany accounts and transactions have been 
eliminated upon consolidation.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT 
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">(d) Producing Oil and Natural Gas 
Properties </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-
indent:8%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">At the time the Trust was 
established, no determinable market value was available for the assets 
transferred to the Trust; consequently, nominal values were assigned. 
Accordingly, no allowance for
depletion has been computed. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-
bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2">Tidelands&#146; revenues are derived from production payments and 
overriding royalty interests
related to properties located in the Gulf of Mexico. </FONT></P> <P 
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">(e) Federal Income Taxes </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">No provision has been made for Federal income taxes on the 
Trust&#146;s income&nbsp;because such taxes are the liability of the 
unitholders.</FONT></P>
<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">Federal income taxes are provided on the income of Tidelands 
Corporation (which specifically excludes the
95% net profits interest to be retained by and&nbsp;delivered to the Trust) 
after deducting statutory depletion. There were no significant deferred tax 
assets or liabilities as of December&nbsp;31, 2011 and 2010. Tidelands 
Corporation uses the cash
method of reporting for Federal income taxes. The primary difference between the
actual tax expense of Tidelands Corporation and the expected tax expense is due
to the fact that only 5% of Tidelands Corporation&#146;s income (i.e., excluding
the 95%
net profits interest retained by and delivered to the Trust) is subject to 
Federal income tax. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-
bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Tax positions 
taken by the Trust related to
the Trust&#146;s pass-through status and Federal state tax positions have been 
reviewed, and the Trustee is of the opinion that material positions taken would 
more likely than not be sustained by examination. In accordance with the 
Trust&#146;s
basis of accounting discussed in Note 1, the Trust would only recognize the 
impact of tax positions that were not upheld at the time of payment. As of 
December&nbsp;31, 2011, the Trust&#146;s tax years 2007 to 2010 remain subject 
to examination.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Federal income taxes refundable which arose
during the prior year are as a result of payments previously made in excess of 
the estimated
taxes payable. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT 
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Tidelands Corporation recognizes 
interest and penalties related to unrecognized tax benefits in income tax 
expense.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT 
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">(f) Credit Risk Concentration and 
Cash Equivalents </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-
indent:8%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Financial instruments which 
potentially subject the Trust and Tidelands Corporation to concentrations of 
credit risk are primarily investments in cash equivalents. The Trust and 
Tidelands Corporation
place their cash investments with financial institutions that the Trustee 
considers creditworthy and limit the amount of credit exposure from any one 
financial institution. The estimated fair values of cash equivalents approximate
the carrying
values due to the short term nature of these financial instruments. </FONT></P> 
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">Tidelands had cash equivalents of $950,422 and $1,299,734 at
December&nbsp;31, 2011 and 2010, respectively, which consisted of cash deposits,
U.S. Treasury and agency bonds, and money market mutual funds. </FONT></P> <P 
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">(g) Use of Estimates </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The preparation of financial statements in 
conformity with
the modified cash basis method of accounting requires the Trustee to make 
various estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amount of liabilities
at the date of the consolidated financial statements and the reported amount of 
expenses
during the reporting period.&nbsp;Actual results may differ from such estimates.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT 
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">(h) Distributable Income per Unit
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT 
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Distributable income per unit is 
determined by dividing distributable income by the number of units of beneficial
interest
outstanding during the period. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-
bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2">(i) Significant Royalty Sources </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The following table presents the approximate 
percentage of royalties actually received from each royalty payor for the past 
three years:
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-
bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" 
CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2"><B>(2)</B></FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2"><B>BASIS OF ACCOUNTING </B></FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-
top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2">The financial
statements of Tidelands have been prepared on the modified cash basis method and
are not intended to present financial position and results of operations in 
conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States
(&#147;GAAP&#148;). Under the modified cash basis method: </FONT></P> <P 
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" 
CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="9%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times 
New Roman" SIZE="2">Royalty income is recognized when received by Tidelands. 
</FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" 
CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="9%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times 
New Roman" SIZE="2">Tidelands&#146; expenses (which include accounting, legal, 
and other professional fees, trustees&#146; fees and out-of-pocket expenses) are
recorded on
an accrual basis. Reserves for liabilities that are contingent or uncertain in 
amount may also be established if considered necessary. 
</FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-
bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" 
CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="9%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times 
New Roman" SIZE="2">Distributions to unitholders are recognized when declared by
the Trustee of the Trust. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The financial statements of Tidelands differ 
from financial statements prepared in conformity with GAAP because of the 
following:
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" 
CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="9%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times 
New Roman" SIZE="2">Royalty income is recognized in the month received rather 
than in the month of production. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" 
CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="9%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times 
New Roman" SIZE="2">Reserves may be established for contingencies that would not
be recorded under GAAP. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">This comprehensive basis of accounting 
corresponds to the accounting principles permitted for royalty trusts by the 
SEC, as specified by
Staff Accounting Bulletin Topic 12:E, Financial Statements of Royalty Trusts. 
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-
family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The preparation of financial statements in 
conformity with the
modified cash basis method of accounting requires the Trustee to make various 
estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amount of liabilities at the 
date of the financial statements and the reported amount of expenses during the 
reporting
period.&nbsp;Actual results may differ from such estimates. </FONT></P> <P 
STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" 
CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New
Roman" SIZE="2"><B>(3)</B></FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2"><B>TEXAS FRANCHISE TAX </B></FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-
top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" 
SIZE="2">Texas does not
impose an income tax. Therefore, no part of the income produced by the Trust is 
subject to state income tax in Texas. However, in May&nbsp;2006, the State of 
Texas enacted legislation, as amended, to implement a new franchise tax. Under 
the new
legislation, a 1% tax (in certain cases not applicable here, the tax rate is 
0.5%) will be imposed on each taxable entity&#146;s taxable margin. Taxable 
margin is generally defined as revenues less certain costs, as provided in the 
statute. Most
entities that provide owners with limited liability protection, including 
trusts, are considered to be taxable entities for purposes of the Texas 
franchise tax. The statute provides certain limited exemptions from the tax, 
including exclusions for
certain &#147;passive entities&#148; that satisfy specified statutory 
requirements as described below. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-
bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Under the Texas 
franchise tax statute,
&#147;passive entities,&#148; including trusts, that meet the following 
requirements, will be exempt from the Texas state franchise tax: (a)&nbsp;the 
trust cannot be a business trust within the meaning of U.S. Treasury Regulation 
section
301.7701-4(b); (b)&nbsp;at least 90% of the trust&#146;s income for the taxable 
year must be derived from passive sources (<I>e.g.</I>, royalties, bonuses, 
delay rental income from mineral properties, dividends, interest, gains from the
sale of
securities); and (c)&nbsp;no more than 10% of the trust&#146;s income for the 
taxable year can be derived from an active trade or business (<I>e.g.</I>, rent,
certain income received by a non-operator under a joint operating agreement 
pursuant to
which the operator is the member of an affiliated group that includes such non-
operator). An entity will determine on an annual basis whether it meets the 
requirements to be treated as a &#147;passive entity&#148; for Texas state 
franchise tax
purposes. The Trustee believes that all or substantially all of the income of 
the Trust currently is passive, as it consists of royalty income from the sale 
of oil and natural gas, dividends and interest income. Subject to any change in 
the sources
of income derived by the Trust or any change in the Indenture, the Trust expects
that it will be a passive entity that is not subject to the franchise tax. 
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">If the Trust is exempt from the 
Texas state franchise tax as a passive entity, each unitholder that is subject 
to the Texas franchise tax as a taxable entity under the Texas Tax Code would 
generally
include its share of the Trust&#146;s revenue in its franchise tax computation. 
The Texas franchise tax does not apply to natural persons. The Trust believes 
that it was a passive entity in 2011. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New 
Roman" SIZE="2">Each unitholder is urged to consult its own tax advisor 
regarding the requirements for filing state tax returns. </FONT></P>
